# Total row sums
fun1 <- function(mat) {
  n <- nrow(mat)
  ans <- double(n) 
  for (i in 1:n) {
    ans[i] <- sum(mat[i, ])
  }
  ans
}
dat <- matrix(rnorm(200 * 100), nrow = 200)

# Cumulative sum by row
fun2 <- function(mat) {
  n <- nrow(mat)
  k <- ncol(mat)
  ans <- mat
  for (i in 1:n) {
    for (j in 2:k) {
      ans[i,j] <- mat[i, j] + ans[i, j - 1]
    }
  }
  ans
}

fun2alt <- function(mat) {
  # YOUR CODE HERE
t(apply(mat,1,cumsum))
  }


# Use the data with this code
set.seed(2315)
dat <- matrix(rnorm(200 * 100), nrow = 200)



# Test for the second
microbenchmark::microbenchmark(
  fun2(dat),
  fun2alt(dat)
)

Problem 2: Make things run faster with parallel computing

sim_pi <- function(n = 1000, i = NULL) {
  p <- matrix(runif(n*2), ncol = 2)
  mean(rowSums(p^2) < 1) * 4
}

# Here is an example of the run
set.seed(156)
sim_pi(1000) # 3.132
## [1] 3.132
# This runs the simulation a 4,000 times, each with 10,000 points
set.seed(1231)
system.time({
  ans <- unlist(lapply(1:4000, sim_pi, n = 10000))
  print(mean(ans))
})
## [1] 3.14124
##  用户  系统  流逝 
## 14.08  2.83 21.59
# YOUR CODE HERE
system.time({
  # YOUR CODE HERE
  ans <- unlist(lapply(1:4000, sim_pi, n = 10000))
  # YOUR CODE HERE
  print(mean(ans))
  # YOUR CODE HERE
})
## [1] 3.142033
##  用户  系统  流逝 
## 12.62  1.03 17.61
library(parallel)
system.time({
  cl <- parallel::makePSOCKcluster(2L)
  parallel::clusterSetRNGStream(cl, 123) # Make sure it is reproducible!
    ans <- parLapply(cl,1:4000, sim_pi, n = 10000)
    print(mean(unlist(ans)))
    parallel::stopCluster(cl)
})
## [1] 3.141365
##  用户  系统  流逝 
##  0.05  0.05 14.14

# install.packages(c("RSQLite", "DBI"))

library(RSQLite)
## Warning: 程辑包'RSQLite'是用R版本4.2.2 来建造的
library(DBI)

# Initialize a temporary in memory database
con <- dbConnect(SQLite(), ":memory:")

# Download tables
film <- read.csv("https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ivanceras/sakila/master/csv-sakila-db/film.csv")
film_category <- read.csv("https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ivanceras/sakila/master/csv-sakila-db/film_category.csv")
category <- read.csv("https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ivanceras/sakila/master/csv-sakila-db/category.csv")

# Copy data.frames to database
dbWriteTable(con, "film", film)
dbWriteTable(con, "film_category", film_category)
dbWriteTable(con, "category", category)
dbListTables(con)
## [1] "category"      "film"          "film_category"
dbGetQuery(con, "PRAGMA table_info(category)")
##   cid        name    type notnull dflt_value pk
## 1   0 category_id INTEGER       0         NA  0
## 2   1        name    TEXT       0         NA  0
## 3   2 last_update    TEXT       0         NA  0
PRAGMA table_info(film)

Question 1 How many many movies is there avaliable in each rating catagory.

Q1<-dbGetQuery(con,"
SELECT   rating,
COUNT(*) AS number
FROM    film
GROUP BY rating
           ")
Q1
##   rating number
## 1      G    180
## 2  NC-17    210
## 3     PG    194
## 4  PG-13    223
## 5      R    195

Question 2 What is the average replacement cost and rental rate for each rating category.

Q2_1<-dbGetQuery(con,"
SELECT  rating, replacement_cost,
COUNT(*) AS count,
AVG(replacement_cost) AS replacement_cost_mean
FROM film
GROUP BY rating
           ")
Q2_1
##   rating replacement_cost count replacement_cost_mean
## 1      G            12.99   180              20.12333
## 2  NC-17            18.99   210              20.13762
## 3     PG            20.99   194              18.95907
## 4  PG-13            28.99   223              20.40256
## 5      R            15.99   195              20.23103
Q2_2<-dbGetQuery(con,"
SELECT  rating, rental_rate,
COUNT(*) AS count,
AVG(rental_rate) AS rental_rate_mean
FROM  film
GROUP BY rating
           ")
Q2_2
##   rating rental_rate count rental_rate_mean
## 1      G        4.99   180         2.912222
## 2  NC-17        2.99   210         2.970952
## 3     PG        0.99   194         3.051856
## 4  PG-13        4.99   223         3.034843
## 5      R        4.99   195         2.938718
Q2<-merge(Q2_1, Q2_2, by.x = "rating", by.y = "rating", all = TRUE)
Q2
##   rating replacement_cost count.x replacement_cost_mean rental_rate count.y

Question 3 Use table film_category together with film to find the how many films there are with each category ID?

Q3<-dbGetQuery(con,"
SELECT  film.film_id, film_category.category_id,
COUNT(*) AS number
FROM film
INNER JOIN film_category  ON film.film_id = film_category.film_id
GROUP BY category_id
")

Question 4 Incorporate table category into the answer to the previous question to find the name of the most popular category.

Q4<-dbGetQuery(con,"
SELECT  film.film_id, film_category.category_id,category.category_id, category.name,
COUNT(*) AS N
FROM film
INNER JOIN film_category  ON film.film_id = film_category.film_id
INNER JOIN category ON category.category_id = film_category.category_id
GROUP BY name 
")
Q4
